## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / continuous-time population dynamics
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is an instantaneous population growth rate, naturally modeled by ordinary differential equations where per-capita growth depends on population size P and possibly time t (environmental change, seasonality, harvesting). With only (t, P) available, classical forms express density dependence, time-varying intrinsic growth, and regulatory/Allee effects as functions multiplying P.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (constant per-capita growth rate in unlimited environment)
- Time-varying intrinsic rate (linear trend): dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (slow environmental drift in per-capita growth)
- Time-varying intrinsic rate (exponential change): dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) * P (accelerating/relaxing change in growth conditions)
- Quadratic density dependence / Verhulst logistic ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (carrying-capacity limitation; c1 ≈ 1/K)
- Logistic with constant harvesting/removal: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (constant quota harvesting or constant mortality flux)
- Logistic with proportional harvesting/mortality: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (extra density-independent per-capita loss)
- Theta-logistic ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) ** c2 (flexible strength/shape of density dependence)
- Gompertz growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (log(c1) - log(P)) (density dependence acts on log-scale; approach to an asymptote)
- Strong Allee effect with crowding: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (negative growth at low P and at high P)
- Weak Allee effect (power-law at low density): dP_dt = c0 * P ** c1 * (1 - c2 * P) (sub/super-linear low-density growth with saturation)
- Seasonally forced growth (per-capita periodicity): dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (seasonal environment modulates per-capita growth)
- Seasonally forced logistic regulation: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P * (1 - c4 * P) (seasonality plus density dependence)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita growth formulation: write (dP_dt / P) = f(P, t); if f is ~constant in P then dynamics are near-exponential, while strong P-dependence implies regulation.
- Carrying-capacity regulation: factors like (1 - c * P) imply a stable equilibrium near P ≈ 1/c where growth changes sign.
- Nonlinear crowding intensity: exponents on the regulation term, (1 - c * P) ** alpha, capture weak vs strong density dependence (alpha > 1 sharper slowdown).
- Allee effects: inclusion of (P - cA) (or low-density power P**alpha with alpha > 1) produces negative/weak growth at small populations and a critical threshold.
- External removals: subtracting c (quota) or c * P (proportional harvest/mortality) shifts equilibria and can create extinction thresholds even when growth is positive at low P.
- Seasonality/environmental forcing: sin(c * t + phase) in the per-capita term produces oscillatory growth rates and can yield cyclic or quasi-cyclic P trajectories.
- Asymptotic approach on log-scale: terms like (log(K) - log(P)) indicate Gompertz-type regulation where relative growth declines roughly linearly with log(P).
- Sign constraints: biologically plausible models often enforce dP_dt → 0 as P → 0 (via multiplicative P), preventing unphysical negative populations under forward integration.
